\ProblemFileHeader{XTL_SV_QUESTIONCOUNT}% Process how many problems are in this file and how to detect if it has a desirable problem
\ifproblemToFind% If it has a desirable problem search the file.
%\tagged{Ans@ShortAns, Type@Compute, Topic@Limit, Sub@Poly, Sub@DifferenceQuotient, File@0022}{
\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${12}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${2}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 12 \, t + 2}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {4}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-124}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={4}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{4},{4}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{4 \, {\left(4 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 3 \, h - 64\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${4}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{4 \, {\left(4 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 3 \, h - 64\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-116}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${9}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${7}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 9 \, t + 7}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {2}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-63}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={2}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{2},{2}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 2\right)}^{2} - 9 \, h - 64}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${2}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 2\right)}^{2} - 9 \, h - 64}{h}} = \answer{-55}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 17 \, h - 144}{h}} = \answer{-79}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${36}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${10}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 36 \, t + 10}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {4}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-100}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={4}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{4},{4}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{4 \, {\left(4 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 9 \, h - 64\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${4}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{4 \, {\left(4 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 9 \, h - 64\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-92}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 31 \, h - 16}{h}} = \answer{-1}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${40}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${8}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 40 \, t + 8}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {3}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-64}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={3}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{3},{3}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{8 \, {\left(2 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 5 \, h - 18\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${3}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{8 \, {\left(2 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 5 \, h - 18\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-56}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left({\left(h + 2\right)}^{2} - h - 4\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-48}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${3}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${6}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 3 \, t + 6}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {3}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-101}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={3}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{3},{3}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 3 \, h - 144}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${3}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 3 \, h - 144}{h}} = \answer{-93}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 5 \, h - 128\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-118}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}

\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${15}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${9}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 15 \, t + 9}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {1}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-25}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={1}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{1},{1}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 15 \, h - 16}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${1}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 15 \, h - 16}{h}} = \answer{-17}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${1}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${9}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + t + 9}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {4}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-135}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={4}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{4},{4}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - h - 256}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${4}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - h - 256}{h}} = \answer{-127}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{

\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${35}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${7}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 35 \, t + 7}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {4}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-101}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={4}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{4},{4}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 35 \, h - 256}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${4}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 35 \, h - 256}{h}} = \answer{-93}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${9}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${7}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 9 \, t + 7}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {3}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-95}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={3}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{3},{3}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 9 \, h - 144}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${3}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 9 \, h - 144}{h}} = \answer{-87}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${27}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${10}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 27 \, t + 10}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {2}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-45}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={2}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{2},{2}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 2\right)}^{2} - 27 \, h - 64}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${2}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 2\right)}^{2} - 27 \, h - 64}{h}} = \answer{-37}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${19}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${9}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 19 \, t + 9}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 19 \, h - 16}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${1}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 19 \, h - 16}{h}} = \answer{-13}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${8}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${7}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 8 \, t + 7}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {3}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-96}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={3}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{3},{3}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{8 \, {\left(2 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - h - 18\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${3}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{8 \, {\left(2 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - h - 18\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-88}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${32}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${3}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 32 \, t + 3}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {4}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-104}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={4}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{4},{4}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left({\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 2 \, h - 16\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${4}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left({\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 2 \, h - 16\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-96}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${38}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${7}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 38 \, t + 7}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {2}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-34}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={2}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{2},{2}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 2\right)}^{2} - 19 \, h - 32\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${2}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 2\right)}^{2} - 19 \, h - 32\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-26}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${7}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${6}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 7 \, t + 6}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={3}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{3},{3}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 7 \, h - 144}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${3}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 7 \, h - 144}{h}} = \answer{-89}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${16}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${3}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 16 \, t + 3}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {3}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-88}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={3}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{3},{3}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left({\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - h - 9\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${3}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left({\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - h - 9\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-80}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${25}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${8}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 25 \, t + 8}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {1}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-15}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={1}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{1},{1}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 25 \, h - 16}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${1}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 25 \, h - 16}{h}} = \answer{-7}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${34}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${4}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 34 \, t + 4}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {4}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-102}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={4}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{4},{4}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 17 \, h - 128\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${4}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 17 \, h - 128\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-94}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${21}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${5}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 21 \, t + 5}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 2\right)}^{2} - 21 \, h - 64}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${2}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 2\right)}^{2} - 21 \, h - 64}{h}} = \answer{-43}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${3}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${8}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 3 \, t + 8}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {2}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-69}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={2}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{2},{2}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 2\right)}^{2} - 3 \, h - 64}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${2}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 2\right)}^{2} - 3 \, h - 64}{h}} = \answer{-61}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${27}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${3}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 27 \, t + 3}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {4}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-109}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={4}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{4},{4}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 27 \, h - 256}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${4}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 27 \, h - 256}{h}} = \answer{-101}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${4}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${0}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 4 \, t}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {3}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-100}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={3}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{3},{3}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{4 \, {\left(4 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - h - 36\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${3}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{4 \, {\left(4 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - h - 36\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-92}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${34}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${6}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 34 \, t + 6}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {4}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-102}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={4}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{4},{4}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 17 \, h - 128\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${4}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 17 \, h - 128\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-94}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${16}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${6}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 16 \, t + 6}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {1}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-24}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={1}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{1},{1}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left({\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - h - 1\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${1}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left({\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - h - 1\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-16}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${8}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${9}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 8 \, t + 9}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {2}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-64}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={2}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{2},{2}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{8 \, {\left(2 \, {\left(h + 2\right)}^{2} - h - 8\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${2}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{8 \, {\left(2 \, {\left(h + 2\right)}^{2} - h - 8\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-56}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${29}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${8}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 29 \, t + 8}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {3}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-75}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={3}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{3},{3}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 29 \, h - 144}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${3}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 29 \, h - 144}{h}} = \answer{-67}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${35}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${4}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 35 \, t + 4}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 35 \, h - 256}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${4}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 35 \, h - 256}{h}} = \answer{-93}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${1}$.}

\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}

%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0

\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${30}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${9}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 30 \, t + 9}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {1}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-10}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={1}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{1},{1}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 15 \, h - 8\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${1}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 15 \, h - 8\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-2}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${26}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${4}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 26 \, t + 4}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {3}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-78}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={3}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{3},{3}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 13 \, h - 72\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${3}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 13 \, h - 72\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-70}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${30}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${7}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 30 \, t + 7}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.

%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 15 \, h - 8\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-2}$

\end{problem}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${5}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${10}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 5 \, t + 10}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {3}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-99}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={3}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{3},{3}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 5 \, h - 144}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${3}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 5 \, h - 144}{h}} = \answer{-91}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${10}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${4}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 10 \, t + 4}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.

$\answer{-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 5 \, h - 8\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${1}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 5 \, h - 8\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-22}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${30}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${5}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 30 \, t + 5}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {3}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-74}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={3}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{3},{3}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 15 \, h - 72\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${3}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 15 \, h - 72\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-66}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${38}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${1}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 38 \, t + 1}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {3}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-66}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={3}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{3},{3}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 19 \, h - 72\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${3}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 19 \, h - 72\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-58}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${34}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${6}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 34 \, t + 6}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.

\begin{multipleChoice}

\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${1}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 17 \, h - 8\right)}}{h}} = \answer{2}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}

\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${30}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${1}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 30 \, t + 1}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {1}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-10}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={1}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{1},{1}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 15 \, h - 8\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${1}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 15 \, h - 8\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-2}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${37}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${2}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 37 \, t + 2}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {1}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-3}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={1}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{1},{1}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 37 \, h - 16}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${1}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 37 \, h - 16}{h}} = \answer{5}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${37}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${0}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 37 \, t}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {1}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-3}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={1}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{1},{1}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 37 \, h - 16}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${1}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 1\right)}^{2} - 37 \, h - 16}{h}} = \answer{5}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${16}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${4}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 16 \, t + 4}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {2}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-56}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={2}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{2},{2}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left({\left(h + 2\right)}^{2} - h - 4\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${2}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left({\left(h + 2\right)}^{2} - h - 4\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-48}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${13}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${9}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 13 \, t + 9}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {4}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-123}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={4}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{4},{4}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 13 \, h - 256}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${4}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 13 \, h - 256}{h}} = \answer{-115}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{

\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${3}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}

%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0

\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${6}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${4}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 6 \, t + 4}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {4}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-130}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={4}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{4},{4}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 3 \, h - 128\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${4}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 3 \, h - 128\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-122}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${16}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${7}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 16 \, t + 7}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {4}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-120}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={4}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{4},{4}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left({\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - h - 16\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${4}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left({\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - h - 16\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-112}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${27}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${1}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 27 \, t + 1}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {3}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-77}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={3}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{3},{3}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 27 \, h - 144}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${3}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 27 \, h - 144}{h}} = \answer{-69}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}

\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${2}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${4}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 2 \, t + 4}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {2}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-70}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={2}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{2},{2}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 2\right)}^{2} - h - 32\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${2}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 2\right)}^{2} - h - 32\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-62}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${14}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${0}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 14 \, t}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {4}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-122}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={4}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{4},{4}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 7 \, h - 128\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${4}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{2 \, {\left(8 \, {\left(h + 4\right)}^{2} - 7 \, h - 128\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-114}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${15}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${8}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 15 \, t + 8}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {3}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-89}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={3}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{3},{3}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 15 \, h - 144}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${3}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{16 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 15 \, h - 144}{h}} = \answer{-81}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}




\latexProblemContent{
\begin{problem}
The position function of a ball thrown into the air with a velocity of ${28}$ ft/sec and initial height of ${0}$ feet is given by the function $s(t) = {-16 \, t^{2} + 28 \, t}$ where $s(t)$ is the height of the ball above the ground after $t$ seconds.  

\input{Limit-Compute-0022.HELP.tex}

Find the average velocity of the ball on the interval starting with $t = {3}$ to the time $0.5$ seconds later. $V_{ave}=\answer[tolerance=0.1]{-76}$

\begin{problem}
Now write an expression for the average velocity of the ball on the time interval from $t={3}$ to $h$ seconds later.  That is, on the interval $[{3},{3}+h]$ where $h\neq 0$. Simplify your answer.  

$\answer{-\frac{4 \, {\left(4 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 7 \, h - 36\right)}}{h}}$

\begin{problem}
How can we (mathematically) determine what happens as $h$ gets closer and closer to 0? 

\begin{multipleChoice}
\choice[correct]{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to 0.}
\choice{We can use limits to find what happens when $h$ goes to ${3}$.}
\choice{We can plug in very small values of $h$ to figure out what the value of $s(t)$ is heading to.}
\choice{We can plug in $h=0$ and then simplify to find an answer.}
\end{multipleChoice}
%average velocity approaches -24 ft/sec as h goes to 0
\begin{problem}
Calculate the limit:

$\lim\limits_{h\rightarrow 0} {-\frac{4 \, {\left(4 \, {\left(h + 3\right)}^{2} - 7 \, h - 36\right)}}{h}} = \answer{-68}$

\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}
\end{problem}}%}
